java.util.Set;\\n48: import java.util.regex.Pattern;\\n49: \\n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\\n51: \\n52: /**\\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\\n54:  * <p>\\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\\\"#consumergroups\\\">consumer groups</a>.\\n58:  * <p>\\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\\\"#multithreaded\\\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\\n62:  *\\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\\n68:  * <p>\\n69:  *\\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\\n79:  * <p>\\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\\n88:  * <p>\\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\\n90:  * detail below.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * <h3><a name=\\\"consumergroups\\\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\\n95:  * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\\n96:  * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\\n98:  * <p>\\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\\n101:  * subscribed topics to one process in each consumer group. This is achieved by balancing the partitions between all\\n102:  * members in the consumer group so that each partition is assigned to exactly one consumer in the group. So if there\\n103:  * is a topic with four partitions, and a consumer group with two processes, each process would consume from two partitions.\\n104:  * <p>\\n105:  * Membership in a consumer group is maintained dynamically: if a process fails, the partitions assigned to it will\\n106:  * be reassigned to other consumers in the same group. Similarly, if a new consumer joins the group, partitions will be moved\\n107:  * from existing consumers to the new one. This is known as <i>rebalancing</i> the group and is discussed in more\\n108:  * detail <a href=\\\"#failuredetection\\\">below</a>. Group rebalancing is also used when new partitions are added\\n109:  * to one of the subscribed topics or when a new topic matching a {@link #subscribe(Pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribed regex}\\n110:  * is created. The group will automatically detect the new partitions through periodic metadata refreshes and\\n111:  * assign them to members of the group.\\n112:  * <p>\\n113:  * Conceptually you can think of a consumer group as being a single logical subscriber that happens to be made up of\\n114:  * multiple processes. As a multi-subscriber system, Kafka naturally supports having any number of consumer groups for a\\n115:  * given topic without duplicating data (additional consumers are actually quite cheap).\\n116:  * <p>\\n117:  * This is a slight generalization of the functionality that is common in messaging systems. To get semantics similar to\\n118:  * a queue in a traditional messaging system all processes would be part of a single consumer group and hence record\\n119:  * delivery would be balanced over the group like with a queue. Unlike a traditional messaging system, though, you can\\n120:  * have multiple such groups. To get semantics similar to pub-sub in a traditional messaging system each process would\\n121:  * have its own consumer group, so each process would subscribe to all the records published to the topic.\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * In addition, when group reassignment happens automatically, consumers can be notified through a {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener},\\n124:  * which allows them to finish necessary application-level logic such as state cleanup, manual offset\\n125:  * commits, etc. See <a href=\\\"#rebalancecallback\\\">Storing Offsets Outside Kafka</a> for more details.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * It is also possible for the consumer to <a href=\\\"#manualassignment\\\">manually assign</a> specific partitions\\n128:  * (similar to the older \\\"simple\\\" consumer) using {@link #assign(Collection)}. In this case, dynamic partition\\n129:  * assignment and consumer group coordination will be disabled.\\n130:  *\\n131:  * <h3><a name=\\\"failuredetection\\\">Detecting Consumer Failures</a></h3>\\n132:  *\\n133:  * After subscribing to a set of topics, the consumer will automatically join the group when {@link #poll(Duration)} is\\n134:  * invoked. The poll API is designed to ensure consumer liveness. As long as you continue to call poll, the consumer\\n135:  * will stay in the group and continue to receive messages from the partitions it was assigned. Underneath the covers,\\n136:  * the consumer sends periodic heartbeats to the server. If the consumer crashes or is unable to send heartbeats for\\n137:  * a duration of {@code session.timeout.ms}, then the consumer will be considered dead and its partitions will\\n138:  * be reassigned.\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * It is also possible that the consumer could encounter a \\\"livelock\\\" situation where it is continuing\\n141:  * to send heartbeats, but no progress is being made. To prevent the consumer from holding onto its partitions\\n142:  * indefinitely in this case, we provide a liveness detection mechanism using the {@code max.poll.interval.ms}\\n143:  * setting. Basically if you don't call poll at least as frequently as the configured max interval,\\n144:  * then the client will proactively leave the group so that another consumer can take over its partitions. When this happens,\\n145:  * you may see an offset commit failure (as indicated by a {@link CommitFailedException} thrown from a call to {@link #commitSync()}).\\n146:  * This is a safety mechanism which guarantees that only active members of the group are able to commit offsets.\\n147:  * So to stay in the group, you must continue to call poll.\\n148:  * <p>\\n149:  * The consumer provides two configuration settings to control the behavior of the poll loop:\\n150:  * <ol>\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1c818d3c-1cfe-48bb-8271-be39144d168f","uuid":"a8a6c11b-04ae-450a-be7d-aac2fd6acf1e","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\\n3:  * contributor license agreements. It is discussed in further\\n90:  * detail below.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * <h3><a name=\\\"consumergroups\\\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\\n93:  *\\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\\n95:  * processing records. All consumer instances\\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\\n98:  * <p>\\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\\n101:  * subscribed topics to one process in each consumer group. This is achieved by balancing the partitions between all\\n102:  * members in the consumer group so that each partition is assigned to exactly one consumer in the group. So if there\\n103:  * is a topic with four partitions, and a consumer group with two processes, each process would consume from two partitions.\\n104:  * <p>\\n105:  * Membership in a consumer group is maintained dynamically: if a process fails, the partitions assigned to it will\\n106:  * be reassigned to other consumers in the same group. Similarly, if a new consumer joins the group, partitions will be moved\\n107:  * from existing consumers to the new one. This is known as <i>rebalancing</i> the group and is discussed in more\\n108:  * detail <a href=\\\"#failuredetection\\\">below</a>. Group rebalancing is also used when new partitions are added\\n109:  * to one of the subscribed topics or when a new topic matching a {@link #subscribe(Pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribed regex}\\n110:  * is created. The group will automatically detect the new partitions through periodic metadata refreshes and\\n111:  * assign them to members of the group.\\n112:  * <p>\\n113:  * Conceptually you can think of a consumer group as being a single logical subscriber that happens to be made up of\\n114:  * multiple processes. As a multi-subscriber system, Kafka naturally supports having any number of consumer groups for a\\n115:  * given topic without duplicating data (additional consumers are actually quite cheap).\\n116:  * <p>\\n117:  * This is a slight generalization of the functionality that is common in messaging systems. To get semantics similar to\\n118:  * a queue in a traditional messaging system all processes would be part of a single consumer group and hence record\\n119:  * delivery would be balanced over the group like with a queue. Unlike a traditional messaging system, though, you can\\n120:  * have multiple such groups. To get semantics similar to pub-sub in a traditional messaging system each process would\\n121:  * have its own consumer group, so each process would subscribe to all the records published to the topic.\\n122:  * <p>\\n123:  * In addition, when group reassignment happens automatically, consumers can be notified through a {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener},\\n124:  * which allows them to finish necessary application-level logic such as state cleanup, manual offset\\n125:  * commits, etc. See <a href=\\\"#rebalancecallback\\\">Storing Offsets Outside Kafka</a> for more details.\\n126:  * <p>\\n127:  * It is also possible for the consumer to <a href=\\\"#manualassignment\\\">manually assign</a> specific partitions\\n128:  * (similar to the older \\\"simple\\\" consumer) using {@link #assign(Collection)}. In this case, dynamic partition\\n129:  * assignment and consumer group coordination will be disabled.\\n130:  *\\n131:  * <h3><a name=\\\"failuredetection\\\">Detecting Consumer Failures</a></h3>\\n132:  *\\n133:  * After subscribing to a set of topics, the consumer will automatically join the group when {@link #poll(Duration)} is\\n134:  * invoked. The poll API is designed to ensure consumer liveness. As long as you continue to call poll, the consumer\\n135:  * will stay in the group and continue to receive messages from the partitions it was assigned. Underneath the covers,\\n136:  * the consumer sends periodic heartbeats to the server. If the consumer crashes or is unable to send heartbeats for\\n137:  * a duration of {@code session.timeout.ms}, then the consumer will be considered dead and its partitions will\\n138:  * be reassigned.\\n139:  * <p>\\n140:  * It is also possible that the consumer could encounter a \\\"livelock\\\" situation where it is continuing\\n141:  * to send heartbeats, but no progress is being made. To prevent the consumer from holding onto its partitions\\n142:  * indefinitely in this case, we provide a liveness detection mechanism using the {@code max.poll.interval.ms}\\n143:  * setting. Basically if you don't call poll at least as frequently as the configured max interval,\\n144:  * then the client will proactively leave the group so that another consumer can take over its partitions. When this happens,\\n145:  * you may see an offset commit failure (as indicated by a {@link CommitFailedException} thrown from a call to {@link #commitSync()}).\\n146:  * This is a safety mechanism which guarantees that only active members of the group are able to commit offsets.\\n147:  * So to stay in the group, you must continue to call poll.\\n148:  * <p>\\n149:  * The consumer provides two configuration settings to control the behavior of the poll loop:\\n150:  * <ol>\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java%3FL1-150\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n3:  * contributor license agreements. import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n49: \n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n51: \n52: /**\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n54:  * <p>\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n58:  * <p>\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n62:  *\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n68:  * <p>\n69:  *\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n79:  * <p>\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n88:  * <p>\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. KafkaConsumer.java - main implementation of the new consumer API\n3. ClassicKafkaConsumer.java - older (now classic) implementation still in use\n4. CommitRequestManager.java - handles offset commits\n5. OffsetMetadataManager.java - manages offset metadata on the server side\n6. The new API uses CommitRequestManager for offset commits instead of direct Zookeeper writes\n2. OffsetMetadataManager on the server-side manages offset storage with snapshot registry\n3. SubscriptionState tracks offset positions on the client side\n4. The new API has explicit methods like commitSync() and commitAsync() instead of being implicit in older APIs\n5. KafkaConsumer API\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe old kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector API was deprecated and removed in Apache Kafka 4.0. The modern KafkaConsumer API provides a cleaner interface for consuming messages from Kafka topics with explicit offset management.\\n\\n## Key Implementation Files\\n\\n### Consumer Interface (New API Contract)\\n**File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java`\\n- Defines the contract for consumer implementations\\n- Introduces explicit offset management methods: commitSync(), commitAsync(), position(), committed()\\n- Enables manual partition assignment with assign() and dynamic subscription with subscribe()\\n\\n### KafkaConsumer (Main Implementation)\\n**File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java`\\n- Implements the Consumer<K, V> interface\\n- Delegates to ConsumerDelegate for actual implementation details\\n- Provides public API for subscribing to topics, polling records, and managing offsets\\n- Supports both automatic and manual offset commit strategies\\n\\n### ClassicKafkaConsumer (Legacy Consumer Implementation)\\n**File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java`\\n- Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V>\\n- Represents the older consumer protocol implementation\\n- Still maintains compatibility with classic consumer groups\\n\\n## Offset Management Architecture\\n\\n### Client-Side Offset Tracking\\n\\n**SubscriptionState:**\\n- **File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java`\\n- Tracks the current consumption position for each assigned partition\\n- Maintains knowledge of which offsets have been fetched vs. consumed\\n- Provides FetchPosition information for tracking leader epochs\\n- Uses AutoOffsetResetStrategy to handle offset reset scenarios\\n\\n**CommitRequestManager:**\\n- **File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java`\\n- Manages offset commit requests (both sync and async)\\n- Handles OffsetCommitRequest protocol messages\\n- Supports auto-commit functionality with configurable intervals\\n- Includes retry logic for failed commit attempts\\n- Interacts with CoordinatorRequestManager to find the group coordinator\\n\\n**OffsetsRequestManager:**\\n- **File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetsRequestManager.java`\\n- Manages offset fetch operations when starting consumption\\n- Fetches committed offsets from the broker\\n- Validates consumer positions against broker log state\\n- Uses OffsetsForLeaderEpochClient for validating positions\\n\\n### Server-Side Offset Storage\\n\\n**OffsetMetadataManager:**\\n- **File:** `group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/OffsetMetadataManager.java`\\n- Manages offset storage on the server (coordinator) side\\n- Maintains mapping from group ID → topic-partition → offset\\n- Uses SnapshotRegistry for timeline-based offset history\\n- Handles OffsetCommitRequest and OffsetFetchRequest protocol messages\\n- Stores offset metadata including commit timestamp and custom metadata\\n- Uses TimelineHashMap for supporting offset snapshots at different times\\n\\n### Group Coordination\\n\\n**ConsumerCoordinator:**\\n- **File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java`\\n- Implements AbstractCoordinator for group membership management\\n- Handles rebalancing and partition assignment\\n- Manages heartbeat and group synchronization\\n- Coordinates offset commits with the server\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n### 1. Explicit vs. Implicit Offset Management\\n- **Old API (ConsumerConnector):** Offset management was often automatic and implicit\\n- **New API (KafkaConsumer):** Developers explicitly call commitSync() or commitAsync() to persist offsets\\n- Default behavior supports auto-commit via `enable.auto.commit` config, but it's more transparent\\n\\n### 2. Offset Commit Protocol\\n- **Old API:** Could use either Zookeeper or Kafka brokers for offset storage\\n- **New API:** Always uses the Kafka broker (group coordinator) via OffsetCommitRequest\\n- Uses the Offset Commit protocol with explicit transaction support\\n\\n### 3. Client-Side Offset Tracking\\n- **Old API:** Position tracking was implicit in the consumer fetch process\\n- **New API:** SubscriptionState explicitly tracks:\\n  - Current position (next offset to fetch)\\n  - Committed position (last offset committed to broker)\\n  - Leader epoch information for each partition\\n\\n### 4. Offset Reset Strategy\\n- **Old API:** Handled via zookeeper fallback or simple configuration\\n- **New API:** Uses AutoOffsetResetStrategy enum (EARLIEST, LATEST, NONE)\\n- Implemented in SubscriptionState with explicit validation\\n\\n### 5. Coordinator Discovery\\n- **Old API:** Used Zookeeper for finding the group coordinator\\n- **New API:** Uses FindCoordinatorRequest protocol (FIND_COORDINATOR API)\\n- Implemented via CoordinatorRequestManager\\n\\n### 6. Offset Metadata Storage\\n- **Old API:** Stored minimal offset information\\n- **New API:** OffsetAndMetadata includes:\\n  - Offset value\\n  - Commit timestamp\\n  - Custom metadata string\\n  - Leader epoch (for new protocol)\\n\\n### 7. Rebalancing and Offset Safety\\n- **New API:** Provides ConsumerRebalanceListener callback for application-level offset management\\n- Supports CommitFailedException to detect rebalances during offset commit attempts\\n- Provides better control over what happens to offsets during rebalancing\\n\\n## Implementation Chain for Offset Commit\\n\\n1. Application calls KafkaConsumer.commitSync(offsets) or commitAsync(offsets)\\n2. KafkaConsumer delegates to ClassicKafkaConsumer (via ConsumerDelegate)\\n3. CommitRequestManager sends OffsetCommitRequest to broker\\n4. Broker's OffsetMetadataManager receives the request\\n5. OffsetMetadataManager stores the committed offset with metadata in the internal __consumer_offsets topic\\n6. CommitRequestManager receives OffsetCommitResponse and invokes callback\\n\\n## Implementation Chain for Offset Fetch\\n\\n1. Application calls KafkaConsumer.poll()\\n2. ClassicKafkaConsumer checks if all partitions have valid positions\\n3. OffsetsRequestManager may fetch committed offsets if needed\\n4. ConsumerCoordinator returns committed offsets from broker\\n5. SubscriptionState updates position information\\n6. Consumer then fetches records from the set positions\\n\\nThe new API provides much clearer separation of concerns, explicit offset management control, and better support for exactly-once semantics through transaction-aware offset commits.\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6558,"cache_read_input_tokens":108033,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6558},"output_tokens":7,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1c818d3c-1cfe-48bb-8271-be39144d168f","uuid":"acfaffc6-d536-4d3c-80f0-dfd815911bc6"}

`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java`\\n- Implements AbstractCoordinator for group membership management\\n- Handles rebalancing and partition assignment\\n- Manages heartbeat and group synchronization\\n- Coordinates offset commits with the server\\n\\n## Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n### 1. Explicit vs. Implicit Offset Management\\n- **Old API (ConsumerConnector):** Offset management was often automatic and implicit\\n- **New API (KafkaConsumer):** Developers explicitly call commitSync() or commitAsync() to persist offsets\\n- Default behavior supports auto-commit via `enable.auto.commit` config, but it's more transparent\\n\\n### 2. Offset Commit Protocol\\n- **Old API:** Could use either Zookeeper or Kafka brokers for offset storage\\n- **New API:** Always uses the Kafka broker (group coordinator) via OffsetCommitRequest\\n- Uses the Offset Commit protocol with explicit transaction support\\n\\n### 3. Client-Side Offset Tracking\\n- **Old API:** Position tracking was implicit in the consumer fetch process\\n- **New API:** SubscriptionState explicitly tracks:\\n  - Current position (next offset to fetch)\\n  - Committed position (last offset committed to broker)\\n  - Leader epoch information for each partition\\n\\n### 4. Offset Reset Strategy\\n- **Old API:** Handled via zookeeper fallback or simple configuration\\n- **New API:** Uses AutoOffsetResetStrategy enum (EARLIEST, LATEST, NONE)\\n- Implemented in SubscriptionState with explicit validation\\n\\n### 5. Coordinator Discovery\\n- **Old API:** Used Zookeeper for finding the group coordinator\\n- **New API:** Uses FindCoordinatorRequest protocol (FIND_COORDINATOR API)\\n- Implemented via CoordinatorRequestManager\\n\\n### 6. Offset Metadata Storage\\n- **Old API:** Stored minimal offset information\\n- **New API:** OffsetAndMetadata includes:\\n  - Offset value\\n  - Commit timestamp\\n  - Custom metadata string\\n  - Leader epoch (for new protocol)\\n\\n### 7. Rebalancing and Offset Safety\\n- **New API:** Provides ConsumerRebalanceListener callback for application-level offset management\\n- Supports CommitFailedException to detect rebalances during offset commit attempts\\n- Provides better control over what happens to offsets during rebalancing\\n\\n## Implementation Chain for Offset Commit\\n\\n1. Application calls KafkaConsumer.commitSync(offsets) or commitAsync(offsets)\\n2. KafkaConsumer delegates to ClassicKafkaConsumer (via ConsumerDelegate)\\n3. CommitRequestManager sends OffsetCommitRequest to broker\\n4. Broker's OffsetMetadataManager receives the request\\n5. OffsetMetadataManager stores the committed offset with metadata in the internal __consumer_offsets topic\\n6. CommitRequestManager receives OffsetCommitResponse and invokes callback\\n\\n## Implementation Chain for Offset Fetch\\n\\n1. Application calls KafkaConsumer.poll()\\n2. ClassicKafkaConsumer checks if all partitions have valid positions\\n3. OffsetsRequestManager may fetch committed offsets if needed\\n4. ConsumerCoordinator returns committed offsets from broker\\n5. SubscriptionState updates position information\\n6. Consumer then fetches records from the set positions\\n\\nThe new API provides much clearer separation of concerns, explicit offset management control, and better support for exactly-once semantics through transaction-aware offset commits.\\n\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
